Free Talk

A Laughing Matter

— Seafarer

Bride: We received quite a few wedding gifts this time. Even Mr. Wang, our neighbor to the west, sent a very large flower basket. We are very grateful for that.

Groom: Ah, that's because when his wife passed away last time, I sent him a very large wreath and went to offer my condolences. This time I'm getting married, so he sent me a very large flower basket. He even came to offer his condolences the night before the wedding. We are old friends who have been through thick and thin!

Tram Conductor (very politely to an old lady): Madam, Hongfu Street is almost here. Aren't you getting off here? Be careful, be careful.

Old Lady: Ah, is Hongfu Street here? Please stop in front of number thirteen.

Tram Conductor: Okay, let me discuss it with the driver. Would you like me to help you down and knock on the door for you?

A: Mr. C's daughter has graduated from the Conservatory of Music and practices singing at home every day.

B: Does she sing soprano or alto?

A: She sings soprano.

B: Then her throat must be hoarse these days.

A: Her throat isn't hoarse, but the ears of everyone in her family have been deafened by her!

A Tale of Reunion

— Qizhen

Yesterday, I attended the wedding banquet of my clan member Zuo Sheng. Someone who knew the love story of the newlyweds told it vividly. It was so tragic and extraordinary that all the guests were moved. I am recording it to tell the readers.

Fate Brings Them Together: Sheng has been working in a certain institution in Xindu for several years. He traveled to Jinshan and Jiaoshan some years ago and stayed at a friend's house. The friend was originally from Dantu, and his wife taught at a certain girls' school in that town. Therefore, there was no shortage of beautiful students among the pupils. Through the introduction of his friend's wife, Sheng met a Miss Xu. The girl was gentle and intelligent, and Sheng was attracted to her. He often invited her to go out together, and the girl did not refuse. After a long time, they became close. After a ten-day trip to Pingyuan, when they returned, the girl saw him off at the station, and they parted reluctantly. Zhenjiang and Ningzhen were not far apart, and the transportation was convenient. It only took half a day to go back and forth. Since Sheng knew the girl, he took a train to Zhenjiang every holiday to see her. Sometimes they questioned each other, analyzed difficulties, and discussed their studies, or they climbed mountains and rivers together, like lovebirds, their happiness was harmonious. After several months, their hearts were in harmony, so they swore an oath to the mountains and seas and vowed to be together forever.

Turbulence in the Sea of Love: That summer, the girl graduated and lived in Shanghai. Their communication gradually decreased. Sheng was about to ask a matchmaker to propose to the girl's family when he suddenly received a letter from the girl, saying that she had recently been informed by her family that she had been promised to a Mr. Liu from Hanjiang. It was difficult to disobey her parents' orders, so she asked him to look for another good match as soon as possible. If fate was not exhausted, they would meet in Yan Jin again. Sheng was shocked as if he had heard a thunderbolt in the clear sky. He was so surprised that he almost fainted several times. The next day, he went to Shanghai to visit the girl. However, the girl had gone to Wumen with her mother to visit relatives a few days ago. Sheng waited for a long time but she did not return, so he went back disappointed. After that, although Sheng repeatedly sent letters, he received no reply. When he went to Shanghai again, the phoenix had left the building and the girl's family had moved. At this point, Sheng was depressed and unhappy, and all his thoughts were extinguished. After two years, he still did not get married, because he could not forget the girl.

Illness Plays Cupid: Worry can hurt the body. Sheng was so obsessed with thinking about the girl day and night that he fell ill. He was confined to his bed, but his illness was in his heart, and medicine was of little help. So he asked for leave and returned to Shanghai to stay. At that time, his residence had just been moved. Sheng lived in the pavilion, and after lingering for more than a month, he showed no signs of recovery. One night, when the night was deep and quiet, and it was close to midnight, Sheng woke up from a dream of missing her, and his tears wet his pillow. Suddenly, he heard the sound of reading aloud, clear and melodious. Listening carefully, it seemed familiar. He couldn't help but feel curious and struggled to get up. He pushed open the window and looked out. He saw that the stars were sparse and the moon was bright, shining like a painting. A young woman on the opposite building was leaning against the window, reading a book under the moon. Her appearance and hair looked like Miss Xu. He looked at her for a long time and wanted to call out, but he was afraid of being presumptuous, so he did not dare to act rashly. The next morning, he asked his family to inquire, saying that this was a Mr. Liu from Hanjiang, the owner of the house had passed away, and all that was left was an aunt and a daughter-in-law. The daughter-in-law, Miss Xu, was still young and a recent widow, not yet a year since her husband's death. Sheng was overjoyed to hear that the person he saw last night was indeed Miss Xu, and his illness gradually improved.

Heaven Grants Their Wish: In a few days, Sheng's illness suddenly disappeared. He eagerly wanted to meet the girl, so he closed the window and waited for her. He finally met her. At that time, they were both overjoyed and sad. For a long time, they could not say a word. The girl thought that Sheng was dead and had been living as a widow out of guilt. Sheng returned to Dadu to work and went back to see the girl every month. They often talked about marriage, but the girl always felt that she was not perfect enough and was ashamed to be Sheng's wife, and that the family was old-fashioned and things were not easy. Therefore, she strongly advised Sheng to marry someone else first, and wait for an opportunity to be a concubine to serve him. However, Sheng was deeply in love and did not want to do so. He vowed to remain single and wait for her for the rest of his life. Years passed, and five years had passed. Sheng and the girl had been guarding each other for several years. Recently, the girl obtained the permission of her parents, and the couple was finally able to become husband and wife.

A Farewell Banquet for Mr. Doya Jukou [土屋計左右]

— Yu Jianhua

Mr. Doya Jukou, the general manager of the Shanghai Mitsui Bank for many years, has been dedicated to Chinese and Japanese art. He has now been promoted to the Tokyo head office and will soon return home with honor. Chinese and Japanese people have been hosting farewell banquets for him for days. On the evening of the 5th, the Japanese Consul General in Shanghai, Mr. Shigemitsu Aoi, hosted a banquet at his private residence at 15 Seymour Road. On the Japanese side, there were Deputy Consul Tanaka, the Oriental Culture Committee member Sakai Yosamichi, Hayashi Izukenjiro, Funatsu Tatsuiro, and Sato Yasunosuke. On the Chinese side, there were mostly famous figures in the art world, including Wang Yiting, Di Chuqing, Huang Binhong, Zhang Shanzi, Qian Shoutie, Yu Jifan, Wang Yingbin, Li Yunshu, Li Zuhan, and Wang Caizun, totaling two tables. The dishes were vegetarian dishes from Jue Lin, with a total of 30 flavors, which were very exquisite. Because Mr. Li is the owner of Jue Lin and has many vegetarian dishes, Mr. Yunshu invented a variety of dishes, so we were able to enjoy the delicious food. During the dinner, we talked about the age of the people present. Mr. Binhong was the oldest at our table, followed by Yunshu, then Sakai Yosamichi, and Shoutie was the youngest. Tanaka happened to be forty years old, and people encouraged him to celebrate his birthday. He mentioned that Japanese birthday celebrations are different from Chinese ones. Chinese people celebrate big birthdays every ten years, while Japanese people only celebrate forty-one and sixty-one. It is said that forty-one is an unlucky year, and sixty-one is a full cycle of the zodiac. Japanese men especially dislike nineteen years old, and women dislike twenty-five years old. Every time they reach that year, they avoid talking about it. Northern China also avoids forty-one, and even uses it as a curse. In Jiangsu and Zhejiang, women marrying at eighteen are considered unlucky. This is similar to Westerners' dislike of thirteen, and is equally incomprehensible. Caizun's appearance, figure, speech, and behavior are very similar to Japanese people. Those who meet him for the first time often misunderstand him. On the other hand, Tanaka and Sakai Yosamichi are very similar to Chinese people. Sakai Yosamichi has been in China for 40 years and has traveled all over the country. The qualifications of Zuhan, Shoutie, and I, who are all under forty, are actually inferior to him. After the banquet, we followed the usual practice of painting for the host. Mr. Yiting wrote "Pine and Crane Longevity", the pine needles were written with continuous strokes, which looked like the letters M W V N in English. Then Mr. Binhong wrote a landscape painting, Mr. Chuqing wrote bamboo. I was in Jiangwan and eager to go home first, so I wrote a narcissus and left.

Chrysanthemum Anecdotes at the Three Friends

— Jingwen

The autumn wind is howling, and the chrysanthemums are in full bloom. The Three Friends Industrial Company's factory has built a chrysanthemum garden next to Mayushan Road in Pudong, covering tens of acres and cultivating tens of thousands of chrysanthemums. All kinds of famous chrysanthemums are gathered here, making a spectacular sight. Now that the chrysanthemum garden is open to the public, ladies and gentlemen flock to visit. The main entrance of the chrysanthemum garden is made of red chrysanthemums in the shape of a triangle, with white chrysanthemums at the bottom. The outer circle has a diameter of ten zhang [~33 meters], and the characters "Three Friends" are formed with yellow chrysanthemums, each character about five zhang [~16.5 meters] square, which is truly a spectacle. Here are some anecdotes from the garden to amuse you.

Mr. Yu Youren Strokes His Beard and Smiles: Yesterday afternoon, Central Committee member Yu Youren arrived gracefully in a car with a total of four people. In addition to Yu, there were also Mr. Yuan Chunyu, Mr. Zeng Tongyi, and Ms. Qi Xiaofeng. Everyone personally signed the visitor's registration book. After Yu entered the garden, he took a look and saw that the famous flowers were competing to please the eye. He couldn't help but sigh, "What a magnificent sight!" When he went to the inner garden and saw the black chrysanthemums and green chrysanthemums blooming together, he praised again, "What a flowery world!" Ms. Xiaofeng said to Yu, "Can I ask for a pot or two of these chrysanthemums?" Yu quickly stopped her and said, "If everyone wants them, there will be nothing left to display." The words were heard by the garden's receptionist, who stepped forward and declared that he was willing to give a few pots for them to enjoy. Yu stroked his beard and smiled in return.

Yue Zhenbao Wields His Brush for the Guests: Mr. Yue Zhenbao, a well-known figure in the business world, went to the chrysanthemum garden yesterday and happened to meet Mr. Zhao Heqing, a famous scholar from Hunan. They entered the rest room together. Zhao wrote a poem to commemorate the occasion: "With their dazzling colors and graceful shapes, they overcome the west wind with their proud bones. Except for Tao Yuanming, few people understand them. The Three Friends endure the cold season together." Mr. Yue immediately wrote a poem in response and wielded his brush for the guests. His calligraphy was quite exquisite and superior to many other wealthy merchants.

Purchasing Gift Certificates With Extravagance: A certain wealthy man visited the garden and happened to be received by Mr. Xu Qixiang, who was in charge of the garden. Mr. Xu was graceful and eloquent, and was known as a social butterfly. He explained the various famous flowers to the wealthy man in detail. When he saw a potted stand of chrysanthemums, the wealthy man liked it very much. However, the chrysanthemum required the purchase of one hundred yuan worth of Three Friends gift certificates to be given away. Although the wealthy man was rich, he was stingy with his money. Now, he actually bought one hundred yuan worth of gift certificates under the lotus tongue of the social butterfly and carried the chrysanthemum away, which can be considered extravagant.

Postscript on the Yishe Rehearsal

— Juyin

Friends in the ticket circle say that the Yishe troupe has a long history in the Shanghai ticket world and that each rehearsal has garnered praise. This is because the person in charge handles things perfectly, there are many talented people, and the results are naturally not weak. This seventh rehearsal was extraordinarily lively, and there are many noteworthy details about the situation at the time. I will pick up a few to leave a mark.

Qiao Mengmei, Skilled in Civil and Military Roles: Mr. Qiao plays Empress He scolding the court. His voice is broad and his breath is full, so he sings the slow tempo and the quick tempo with ease from beginning to end. In the evening, he plays the City of Sizhou and fights with Sun Wukong. His skills are skilled, unhurried, and very interesting to watch. The two plays are civil and military, each excelling in its own way.

Two Great Ticket Holders Showcase Their Skills: One of the two ticket holders is Ni Qiuping, a well-known name in Shanghai, and the other is Wang Ruoqi. On this day, in deference to Mr. Wang Zhexiang's request, he performed Chang'e Flies to the Moon. The first scene began with a slow tempo and the first phrase, which won a lot of applause. Mr. Wang's singing was also full of charm. The Southern Bangzi excerpt was especially worth savoring. The rest, such as the posture, costume, and waist work, were all excellent. This play was created by Mei Lanfang and is one of the ancient costume plays. It was unexpected to see it performed by amateur actors, and I was fortunate to witness it.

Shi Zhendong, Excellent in Both Male and Female Roles: Shi Zhendong is a pillar of the Yishe troupe. The play he performed on that day was Saying Goodbye to Xue Pinggui. His posture was very characteristic. His posture during the farewell was composed and calm, which can be described as steady and experienced. In the evening, he transformed into a princess in the play Visiting Mother and Inquiring Minds. His slow tempo and the flowing water of the oath were sweet and round, closely resembling Hui Sheng. Mr. Shi Zhendong excels in both male and female roles.

The Entire Cast Performs the Imperial Stele Pavilion: Finally, Mr. Zeng Manjun and Mr. Zhai Zhifu performed the full version of the Imperial Stele Pavilion. Mr. Zeng's Wang Youdao's voice was high and bright, his words were accurate, and his melody was rounded. His costume and stage steps were also natural and unrestrained. The excerpt from the Western Leather Original Board at the time of writing the divorce letter was especially wonderful. Unfortunately, the rest of the excerpts were covered by strange noises, so I couldn't hear them, which was very annoying. Although Mr. Zhai's Meng Yuehua's costume was mediocre, his performance was very skilled. The two sliding steps when avoiding the rain and the frightened look when Wang Youdao rebuked her were vividly portrayed, as if she was in the scene. Moreover, the entire play did not use a professional troupe, and all the supporting roles were performed by troupe members, each contributing their own strengths, which was especially commendable.

New World's Literary Riddles Flourish

— Yanzi

The New World Amusement Park is the ultimate place for recreation and sorrow relief in Shanghai. Since its internal renovation, it has attracted various high-end entertainment and is welcomed by the upper class. During this autumn festival, rare chrysanthemums of various kinds are on display, with extremely gorgeous colors. On the third floor, there is also a Literary Riddles Society, which is hosted by senior figures in the literary world such as Wu Lianzhou, He Yaoqiao, and Zhegen Laoren. Every evening (8 pm to 10 pm), figures in the literary world such as He Wanzhuan, Dong Han and others gather on the first floor to deliberate, guess, and enjoy themselves. Here are the revealed riddle clues: Buying Rouge - Beijing Opera name (花王破鈔打京戲名一) - (买胭脂) Dynasty - Divides into 2-4-6 (二四六分明打字一) - (朝) Grumbling - Literary Phrase (仄聲打文言一句) - (不平则鸣) Ingenious Marriage - Chinese character (巧姻緣打字一) - (柯) Must be With Daily - Historical Figure (一日不可無此君打古人一馬尾卷簾格) - (王旦) Qing Dynasty Servants Submit - Five Tang poem line (大清入關侫臣紛紛投降打五唐一) - (不才明主弃) Impoverished Field Dweller - Five Tang poem line (卑田院中人打五唐一) - (同是長干人) Defeat Many Miles of Waves - Book of Poetry Quote (能破萬里浪者有幾打詩品一) - (寥寥长风) Identifying Concubine Xu - New Play (畫圖省識徐妃面打新劇名一) - (半張小照) Actor Arrested - Beijing Opera (名丑被押打京劇一) - (趕三關) Li Bai to the Heaven - Plant Name (李謫仙直上靑雲打植物名二) - (白果凌霄) Watching Drill in Court - Three Kingdoms Person (在内廷觀操打三國人名一) - (于禁陳武) Practicing Plum Blossom Formation - Three Kingdoms Person (操演梅花陣打三國人名一秋千格) - (伍習) Intimidating General and King - Book of Poetry Quote (赳赳武夫氣凛凛大王風打詩品一) - (积健为雄) Ancient Slanting Sun - Five Tang poem line (千古弔斜陽打五唐一) - (落日故人情)

These are Wu Nizhou, He Wanzhuan, Dong Han's prized work and many people enjoyed guessing them.

Customers who spend one yuan or more will still receive a set of "Lingbo Qianying" moving pictures. Received ten sets yesterday, hereby acknowledged.

West Lake Impressions (III)

— Huijian

On the 7th, I got up at 7 a.m. and went to the Lakeside Park to find the boatman from yesterday. He took us by boat to the south, first to the Orioles Singing in the Willows. The place is very close to Yongjin Gate, and the thousand willows on the water present a different scenery. In the pavilion in the east, there is a huge stone tablet with the inscription "Orioles Singing in the Willows" in red letters, which was written by Emperor Kangxi of the Qing Dynasty. The Zou Youqian Wang Temple was built by the people of Zhejiang to worship Qian Miao. The temple is magnificent, and looking north from the temple embankment, the scenery of the lake seems to have a wonderful structure. Banxia said that the willows drooping in the clear autumn water deserve to be one of the ten scenic spots. The imperial boat went further west to the Three Pools Mirroring the Moon. A boy was on the boat to collect water chestnuts, so we went there first. There are four islands in West Lake: Gushan, which is now connected to the mainland by Bai Causeway, Ruan Dun, Huxin Pavilion, and Three Pools Mirroring the Moon, all of which are isolated in the water and cannot be reached without a boat. Among the three islands, the scenery of the Three Pools Mirroring the Moon is the best. The winding Su Causeway to the west sets it off beautifully. The area is also the widest. The front is the Imperial Stele Pavilion, the back is Xiaoyingzhou, and the middle is a deep pool with a curved bridge built on it, which is very artistic. It turns out that this place was not originally an island, but later a dike was built around the pool. Its completion was man-made rather than natural, which was not easy. Last night, we visited here when it was dark and we could not see everything. Lao Lan insisted on revisiting, so we sat in the Yingxuan Pavilion on the front shore. At noon, we took a boat to Wang Zhuang in Changqiao. The Zhuang was newly built in Western style and belonged to a tea merchant named Wang from Shanghai. The content was not worth seeing. After leaving Wang Zhuang, we went to Chishanbu to disembark. This place is close to Su Causeway and backs against Dingling Mountain. The scenery is very similar to Jiangcun, Gao Zhuang, Jiang Zhuang, and Huagang Guanyu. When we passed Huagang, a young woman and a man were sitting and drinking tea. Gao Zhuang is purely a Chinese old-style building and is adjacent to Huagang. It is the old house of Mr. Gao from Hangzhou, the so-called Hongli Mountain Villa. We entered and saw that the window and pavilion structure were elegant and simple, but it seemed to have been abandoned for a long time. People today feel like they are passing through ruins. About one or two hundred steps from Gao Zhuang is Jiang Zhuang. The boatman said that it was Commander-in-Chief Jiang's villa, but it was actually the villa of Jiang Su'an from Jinling. Su'an was a descendant of Jiang Zi and liked literature very much. This house originally belonged to Lian Nanhu from Wuxi. Lian was troubled by debts, so Jiang bought it for 30,000 gold and slightly renovated it to make it look new. Jiang Jieshi once stayed here when he visited West Lake, so people mistakenly thought it was Jiang's house. There are several famous couplets in the house. Kang Youwei's couplet called Su'an "little friend" and was very interesting. After leaving Jiang Zhuang, the boatman asked if we needed lunch. We agreed, and he recommended the restaurant in front of Liu Zhuang. When we arrived, there were only a few thatched huts and the food was very bad. Entering Liu Zhuang, we found that it was the crown of all the gardens in the lake. There were many kinds of antiques and treasures in the hall. A ink duck marble screen was very eye-catching. On the windows of the back hall, ink vines were used to entangle flowers and landscapes. All the sketches were extremely lifelike. The owner of the Zhuang was a Cantonese man named Liu, who was rich in resources. Behind the Zhuang, he built his own tomb and the tombs of eight concubines were arranged on both sides in the shape of a swallowtail. Banxia said that this gentleman's outlook on life was worth studying.

Gold Market Shows Slight Weakness

Fluctuations Within Two Taels, No Major Gains or Losses: Yesterday, the 8th, the gold market showed a reverse trend after successive gains. The market remained flat in the morning, but weakened around noon. There were no significant gains or losses, with only about two taels of fluctuation. Foreign exchange remained scarce, and banks had slight difficulties in accepting East Asian currencies. Demand and supply varied among dealers. Yuansheng, Yu Da, goods companies, and the Dalian trading group all had both buying and selling activity, as did Yifeng, Yongfu, Changyuan, and Lichang. Prices seemed low in the early morning, but the overseas silver market remained stable and sellers were active. Subsequently, Yuansheng and arbitrageurs made purchases, causing prices to rebound strongly. The market then leveled off. Around noon, sellers increased, and market sentiment became weak, leading to a decline of two taels. The price then reached eighty-two taels. Later, due to the usual weekend market closure, the market was indecisive.

The market fell slightly in the morning by two taels. For delivery in December, the opening price in the morning was 583.5 taels, down 0.5 tael. (The gross price was around 4 taels). Large silver bars and exchange rates remained unchanged. Subsequently, Yifeng and Yongfu sold off, pushing prices down by another 0.5 tael to 83 taels. Soon, Yuancheng and arbitrageurs bought, pushing the price up by 1.0 tael to 84.2 taels. Exchange rates remained stable. Sumitomo bought spot gold, and the Dalian group bought at 1.262 taels. The official rate for January remained unchanged, but the January English gold rate could be settled at 174.375, so the price was 83.9 taels. In a short time, Wanxing, Shunli, Yu Da, and others entered the market to buy, and Zhengjin bought February English gold at 174.375, raising the price by 1.0 tael to 85.1 taels. At this time, Fuchang and individual investors sold off, immediately dropping the price by 7-8 qian. At around 10 o'clock, the price was 4.3-4.4 taels. Soon after, arbitrageurs bought in, adding 0.5-0.6 qian, making the price 4.8-4.9 taels. However, Dongya sold January English gold at 174.375, and the Dalian group sold, dropping the price by 1.0 tael to 3.8 taels in just ten minutes. Then, because the Bank of China and Hua Bi did a deal on the current month's Citibank at 39.25 yuan, the price rebounded by 0.7-0.8 qian to 4.6 taels. At 10:30, the price was 4.6 taels. Hua Bi and Mitsui bought spot gold from the Dalian group at 1.26375 taels. Afterwards, the trend was flat, fluctuating by only a few qian. Around 11 o'clock, the price fell slightly by 0.4-0.5 qian. Then, at 84 taels, the price remained stable for a long time. Suddenly, at 11:45, a storm arose. Daheng Yuan sold off, and other firms followed suit. In just over ten minutes, the price dropped by 1.4-1.5 taels. Market sentiment panicked, and the market fluctuated. At noon, the closing price was 82.8 taels, down 1.2 taels from the previous day. Continued trading for over ten minutes caused the price to drop by less than two taels. The exchange was not responsible for this, and the dealers settled it themselves. The maximum price for the morning session was 5.1 taels, and the minimum price was 2.8 taels, a difference of 2.3 taels. The announced price was still 619.8 taels, with 36-37 taels deducted. The registered amount was 92 taels to 83 taels, with 92 taels used for compensation. The price for commodities in the early market was 3.6 taels, and the closing price was 2 taels.

Different trading behaviors within the market: Among the various firms, Yifeng, Yongfu, Fuchang, Yiheng, Lichang, Hengxing, Taiheng Yuan sold off. Shunli, Wanxing, Yuancheng, Yu Da, and Tongtaichang all bought in. Zhifengyong, Dadecheng, Yuanmaoyong, Senchangyong, Yuanxingyong, and Chunyongyong engaged in both buying and selling, sometimes buying and selling on behalf of customers, so the volume was not small. Arbitrageurs bought up goods. Other firms did not have large orders. The Dalian group was eager to buy, taking in 800 bars and releasing 200 bars. The Guangdong group sold off a small amount.

Prediction of US Cotton Government Report

New York, 7th: The fourth US cotton government estimate will be released on the 8th. Based on various private estimates, the production amount is predicted to be 14,398,000 bales, and the quantity already ginned is 11,000,000 bales.

US Cotton Market Still Not Optimistic

Grain Market Weak, Securities Also Weary

New York, 7th: Reporting on the cotton market situation for the week, the cotton price reaction in the spot market that occurred after the price increases in the second half of October continued this week. After the May futures price reached 12 cents, buying by the industry gradually decreased, with purchases resuming only when prices fell back. In reality, the cotton price increase from the low point in early October has loosened the cotton market's position. When purchases by the industry and short covering gradually subsided, the market price became weak due to selling from the South and profit-taking by bulls. The grain market is weak, securities have also not become firm, and the content of the government cotton production report on November 8 is still uncertain. Therefore, the trend of squaring positions has become more pronounced, intending to wait for future developments. It is doubtful whether the price increases can be sustained before there is a real improvement in trade and a real reduction in cotton fields. Therefore, bullish sentiment is still limited by this kind of doubt.

The domestic inquiry for recent shipments is progressing compared to before, but futures are receiving less attention, especially the 1932 futures, which lack attention. Domestic locking fees remain low. Domestic cloth trading is firmer, but transaction volume is less. The average opinion is that the agricultural ministry's cotton production report will be approximately 14.5 million bales. The weekend statistics are attached below (unit: thousand bales):

Japonica Rice Market: Southern Prices Rise, Northern Prices Stabilize

In Zhabei, the supply from various sectors was slightly better yesterday, with about twenty firms. Sales were slightly dull. After the sharp rise in new japonica rice prices, buying interest waned. High prices remained at 16.2 yuan, and the situation showed a stabilizing trend. The supply of "thin" rice remained weak, and the market remained firm. Top quality opened at 15.7 yuan. The shape of the "yangxian" rice market showed signs of fatigue, with sluggish sales, so it fell by 2 cents, with the top quality opening at 13.5 yuan. "Shejian" rice remained stable and especially high at the 14-yuan mark. Buying interest in port tip rice weakened, and prices decreased slightly, with the highest price at 13.5 yuan. The high price of guest tip rice was barely maintained, while mid-tier rice was reduced by 2-3 cents. Due to rain, transactions were extremely rare throughout the day, and the market felt sluggish.

In South Shanghai yesterday, very little rice arrived by river, and sales in the main streets were sluggish, but market sentiment was very good due to the previous day's price increases. New japonica rice from Changbang rose by 3 cents, with the highest quality requiring the 16-yuan mark. Su-Tong white japonica rice also prospered, rising to 14.8 yuan. "Yangxian" rice opened at around 13 yuan, and "Dujian" rice at 13.3 yuan, both also increasing by 2 cents. Because the source of "xian" rice is very scarce, price increases are inevitable. "Yinyuan" was slightly firm, reaching as high as 11.4 yuan.

Different Views on the Flour Market

Initially Firm, Then Flat, Recent Highs Diverge from Lows

Yesterday, the flour market showed an initial firm and then flat pattern after the opening in the morning and afternoon sessions. The prices of foreign wheat were also good at the opening of each morning, and floating shorts generally scrambled to cover. The factories were all on the sidelines, not making an offer so prices were firmer than the morning. However, the domestic market was still steady, and outside shorts had to start covering. Because wheat imports were not flowing smoothly, insiders and outsiders again found themselves in an impasse, and therefore prices went down again. As a result, this month was up 2.5 mills from the previous day, December up 2.5 mills, January/February down 7.5 mills, March down 2.5 mills, and April down 7.5 mills.

Standard Market Amidst the Arrival of Foreign Wheat

Yesterday, after the opening of wheat futures in the morning and afternoon, all months turned to a firm and stable trend. Foreign wheat prices also increased by 2-3 cents, and the sentiment of insiders and outsiders naturally turned stable. However, because very little local wheat was available this month, although there was a large stockpile of high-quality wheat inland, the combined price did not justify shipping to Shanghai. The chips of the shorts were all supported by foreign wheat. However, it turned out to be difficult in reality, and there was a reason why the sentiment was bullish. However, because Fufeng had another ship of Australian white wheat arriving at around 7,000 tons, and 1,000 tons of it had been purchased by traders and was urgently being sold off, the asking price was 4.9 taels. A certain factory only offered 4.8 taels, and they were still in negotiations. Due to this reason, market sentiment softened slightly again. As a result, November, December, and January were up 2 cents from the previous day, February and March were up 1 cent, and April was up 3 cents.

Dried Goods: Red Dates, Lower-Grade Goods Scarce

The price of Tianjin goods has eased.

Tianjin red dates have continued to arrive recently, and some guest goods have also been released, and prices have gradually become cheaper, and land prices have eased accordingly. The inventory is thicker than before. The market situation for high-grade goods is sluggish, so the market trend for Tianjin head households is weaker. The rest of the second and third households are selling more actively at lower prices. The head household red dates sold in the market yesterday for 10 to 9.5 taels; the second household for 7 to 6.8 taels; the third household for 5 to 4.8 taels. Miscellaneous goods such as Haojiang, Jixin Hong, and Si Hong are scarce. However, Fu Hong was active yesterday, with 260+ packages released at 5.6 taels. Lower-grade goods are scarce, and the market is relatively bullish.

Hardware Market Affected by Autumn Rain

Yesterday's heavy autumn rain greatly affected hardware transactions, as guest businesses mostly stopped buying because they were afraid that shipping and other items would be damaged by water stains. Therefore, transactions were sparse, but fortunately, there were no price fluctuations.

Black Iron Sheets: 3,000 Bundles of New Items Arrived

The shortage of 18-sheet black iron sheets in the market has long been reported in this newspaper, so general buyers are eagerly awaiting them. Yesterday, New Taikoo Wharf had 30 bundles of new goods arriving, so the market situation is expected to be free of shortages in the future. The standard price is currently selling at 11.75 taels.

Silk and Tea: Zhenmei and Pearl Tea Sales Turn Brisk

Yesterday, in the local foreign firm tea market, firms such as British firms Jinlong and Tianxiang started to purchase Zhenmei and Pearl tea, and transactions were quite brisk. However, the silk and tea market has been sluggish for a long time, and tea prices have fallen to the extreme, and market sentiment is weak, making it difficult to reverse the downward trend. There were no major transactions of Gongxi green tea and Qimen black tea by Russian firms yesterday, but the firm has a large sales volume and will continue to search for goods, but it is difficult to expect prices to relax.

Foreign Firms' Silk Sales Increasingly Sluggish

Yesterday was the last day of the autumn races, and the foreign firms' silk market became increasingly sluggish. Yokohama Japanese silk remained sluggish, and overseas silk telegrams to Shanghai were depressed, and the market was depressed. Yesterday, Dachang sold five packages of "Double Child" brand top-grade 13-18 filament silk for 800 taels. Kechang sold twelve packages of Heji first and second grade washed yellow silk for 340 taels.

Seafood: Rumors of a Final Decision on the Ningpo Cuttlefish Market

Although the new production of Ningpo cuttlefish is abundant, the fishermen have united to hoard stocks in order to rectify the market because the selling price is too low. Therefore, the number of goods coming from the mountains has decreased sharply in recent days, and although the purchasing party is preparing to convene the industry to discuss a public distribution to gain profits, a public distribution was decided. Yesterday the internal determination for high grade North Beach cuttlefish price thirty eight taels, commodity goods thirty six taels, large special Ning cuttlefish thirty five taels, average twenty seven and one half taels, secondary goods after rain twenty six taels, the board will convene very soon.

Youth Garden

Northern Journey Impressions

— Su Ling

(Twenty-Two) Returning South

Gang helped me get a free ticket for the Chinese Eastern Railway. Holding this piece of paper that would send me back south, as I walked down the high steps of the council hall, I felt my body was as aimless as a fallen leaf.

Indeed, although I had a free ticket for the Chinese Eastern Railway, my travel expenses were still insufficient. Fortunately, if Qing hadn't found me another five yuan in Japanese currency, my return south would have been further delayed. Thinking about it, how embarrassing.

It suddenly started raining. After saying goodbye to my friends in the clubhouse, Qing accompanied another friend to Beijing at the same time, so he saw me off at the train station.

I put my two worn-out bags from the north onto the train car. Alas, now I have to bring them back to Jiangnan.

After waving goodbye to Qing, the train body lurched forward. Now I have to say to Harbin, "(Farewell, farewell)." I remember saying this when leaving Shanghai. I didn't expect that in just half a year, Shanghai would be seeing me again. This was not what I had originally expected. But this time, it's truly hard to say when I will see Harbin again. However, for someone as rootless as me, it is certainly impossible to say that there is no possibility of returning to the Northeast in the short term. I remember three years ago, in the autumn, I swore never to go to Wuxi again because of a school trip. However, afterwards, I went to Wuxi twice in one month.

The feeling inside the train car was the same as when I came, although once was in winter and the other was in early autumn (actually, it's still mid-summer in Jiangnan). After a night of turbulence, we arrived at Changchun.

Lonely, guarding my two pieces of luggage, sitting in the waiting room, my thoughts were transformed into countless memories of the past, present, and future, hopes, dreams, and even worries.

Before leaving Shanghai, I always dreamed of going to the north. Who knew this was just a dream, a dream of a lonely wanderer. Not only did I not gain or accomplish anything, but I returned south so hastily and embarrassingly. But the biggest question is what to do after returning south. Although I boldly said to my friends in the north, "(Enough, I don't want to stay in the north for another day. Let me go back to the south...)" But what will happen when I return to the south? This big and terrible question haunted me.

(Alas, don't go back to the south. There is nothing to pursue in the south. Friends are scattered, women have long forgotten you, this wandering person, and life is still a huge problem. Then turn back to Harbin, but that is absolutely impossible. Friends will fear you, this person with a nervous breakdown. How about going to Beijing? Perhaps there is a way to live in Beijing...)

However, in the end, I still bought a ticket to Dalian, because maybe I can settle down in Dalian. Didn't Lao Yang's letter say that there was food for me in Dalian? Alas, at this point, one can only look for food for each day.

Boarding the South Manchurian Railway, from the train window, I could see the green fields rushing past. This was different from the impression when I came.

Not far from me, in the seat, was a young Japanese woman. I don't know which station she got on at. She probably had hysteria, or maybe she was a romantic poet. She leaned alone against the window, holding a book in her hand, singing continuously, not Japanese songs, but Western tunes. She was not at all afraid of the gaze of the passengers. Her face was haggard, and her black hair was disheveled.

I spent the entire time on the train watching this young Japanese woman.

It was night, and the train arrived in Dalian. I thought maybe Lao Yang would come to meet me.

Walking out of the train and onto the platform, sure enough, Lao Yang and his new wife were waiting at the station.

I hired a horse-drawn carriage, and Lao Yang, his wife, and my luggage were all taken to Lao Yang's house.

"(Let your return journey south stop in Dalian, my friend)," Lao Yang said to me.

I was silent for a while.

"(I really can't predict my own life)."

To Jiaxing

— Yun He

The sky in the east gradually revealed a fish-belly white, and a patch of white clouds awaited the dyeing of the red sun. At this time, the alumni of the Sociology Department of Fudan University at the Fuxing Society had already climbed out of their very warm beds to prepare for departure.

However, things did not allow us to be very smooth. The students living on campus were still dreaming sweet dreams in their beds. When the friend leading this picnic realized this fact, they went to call them and her to get up until half-past six when they began to urge the car to proceed to the North Station.

This fact gave us a very bad result. When we arrived at the North Station, the whistle had already sounded, clearly telling us that the 7 o'clock express train would not allow us to board. The result of negotiating with the stationmaster was to change to the 9 o'clock express train to He.

Originally, this trip of ours was not purely a trip. The purpose was a picnic. As long as we could play together, we could at least satisfy our desires. So, the waiting room of the train station was temporarily occupied by us as a place for entertainment.

The lonely waiting room was now filled with amiable and happy air. A series of lively dramas will begin here.

Female Students at the Misty Rain Tower

After distributing biscuits and other food like relieving famine victims, we distributed bright flowers to everyone to put on their chests, so that everyone had a smile on their brows. One person suggested that everyone introduce themselves, so Mr. Zhao plagiarized and wrote:

"(I am Zhao Zilong of Changshan)." And Mr. Jin imitated Zhang Sheng's tone in The West Chamber and said:

"(My surname is Jin, my name is ×××, born on × month × day × hour, and I am not yet married)."

It elicited a burst of laughter.

There were two professors, twenty-seven male students, and nine female students on this trip.

It was already half-past eight, and we boarded the train one after another. The thirty-eight people were arranged on both sides of the carriage, as lively as chicks.

In order to avoid the loneliness of the journey, small games began. We divided the students into six groups according to the color of the flowers, and each group had to ask and answer each other once.

"(Mr. Ying, how old are you)?" A student asked.

"(Thirty-four)," our director replied.

"(What about Mrs. Ying)?"

"(Um, one year older)." The whole place laughed.

In another group:

"(Ah Lin, have you been married)?"

"(I have been married and have two children)."

"(What is the name of your wife)?"

"(She is called Huang Juhua)." Everyone laughed so hard they bent over.

The train passed Fanwangdu. Mr. Xiao Yuan pointed out his alma mater, St. John's University, and told us many stories. He returned to his youthful aspirations. He said in a bold tone:

"(The place where the trees are shaded is the football field. I was the Cheerleader during the ball games)."

"(The corner where the red building is located is St. Mary's Girls' School. I often went there to look for people)."

"(Who were you looking for)?" A student asked.

"(Looking for My Sister)." The tone revealed a flaw, and applause thundered.

Time passes most easily in laughter. Half-past eleven had arrived in Jiaxing. The weather was not good, and it was drizzling.

We entered a restaurant called Yanleyuan. We felt a little hungry, so we ate and chewed at the table. Someone in the meal suggested that everyone say a word, and it should be about their own shortcomings. Some said, "(I am missing a tooth)," some said, "(I am nearsighted)." The most solemn of these two sentences was:

"(I am old)," a female student said.

"(As for me, I feel very cold when I see women)," another male student said.

People all have their own memories and their own objects of sadness. No one's life passes without shortcomings.

After the meal, we bought a boat to tour the Misty Rain Tower. Looking out, the misty water was hazy, and the distant trees and fishing boats were faintly visible. In the ancient scenery, we were poets in the daytime.

Without words, without singing, wandering on the painted railings and long corridors, everyone's minds were surrounded by the sky full of misty rain, as if mourning this old tower.

Mr. Xiao's poetic inspiration burst out, and he wrote on paper:

"(Mountain traces and wave shadows meet the lake's level, misty rain is bleak, seeing the ancient city repaired into mandarin ducks (note) cannot get a pair, I want to ask about the next life...)"

Mr. Xiao said, "(I won't continue writing)." This poem contained an unspoken past event.

The small boat drifted towards Luofan Pavilion. On the water journey from Misty Rain Tower to Luofan Pavilion, you can appreciate the famous products of Jiaxing that you admire. This can indeed dispel the loneliness of your journey.

Arriving at Luofan Pavilion, old trees like dragons cover the broken mausoleums and ruined palaces, and fine rain drips on the wutong trees.

In front of Li Bai's Hall, Mr. Xiao proposed to pay homage to the Drunken Old Man. Mr. Xiao loved excitement. He brought a belly full of poetry and wine to the world to seek excitement. No wonder he wanted to praise the banished immortal.

At four o'clock, we visited Xiuzhou Middle School. In the reception room, we learned that the school had been established for more than thirty years. It was said that it was established by the church. The principal was very attentive in leading us to visit the cleanliness of the dormitory and the silence in the library. I couldn't help but recall my past life and today's romance.

At seven o'clock, we took the train back. A fire dragon pierced through the darkness in the rain and brought us back to the palace of the metropolis.

We have returned, we only feel happy and joyful.

Finally, we said that Jiaxing, this old city in Jiangnan, can make us think of the scenery and heroic village songs and the graceful dances of beautiful women described in Ming and Qing novels. It seems that they are all swaying into one piece in the Qionglou Yuyu.

Jiaxing in the rain is indeed imprinted in the minds of our people, a vagueness that will never be forgotten.

Note (The location of Misty Rain Tower, South Lake, is also known as Mandarin Duck Lake)

Page 22

Forgot to Bring Money Shen Dongmei

Her new life began. With the help of a friend, she packed her bags and went to Shanghai to study at a middle school.

These days, she didn't feel troubled. After paying for room and board, she had a ten-yuan bill left. Therefore, in the shortest possible time, she was able to show off a rich and generous scene. In front of many female students, their inexperienced minds thought she was a wealthy woman.

"(Although I am not considered wealthy in Shanghai, I am already unique in my town. My grandfather left me four thousand acres of land and many city houses. Half of the houses in my town are ours. We also opened twelve shops. At the end of each year, the rent, rice, house money, and interest received are truly uncountable. I am very comfortable at home. Now there are so many gangs, so I dare not wear silk clothes or wear valuable jewelry, although there are many of these things in my house)." She often used these words to tell the students all over the school. The students really believed her words.

But this mere ten yuan is easily used up. On the day it was completely used up, she felt depressed. However, soon she thought of a good method.

"Oh, I came out too hastily and forgot to bring money. What I am using now is what I accidentally found in my bag. Although I have written a letter to my family to ask for it, these few days have made me suffer. Like someone who is used to spending like me."

"(What's the big deal? I have dozens of dollars that I can lend you. It's good that your family sends money very quickly and easily)," every student said.

"(It's embarrassing, right? I've never borrowed money before)."

"(Haha, you are really a wealthy young lady. What's so embarrassing about borrowing temporarily? Indeed, in the eyes of a wealthy young lady, borrowing money is very shameful)." Every student thought it was a great honor to lend money to a wealthy young lady.

So she felt happy. As a result, she borrowed two or three hundred yuan from various students.

This was a strange thing. Her clothes were all replaced with new ones.

Time passed quickly. After a month, her money still hadn't arrived.

One afternoon, she sat on the bed in the bedroom, thinking silently, thinking silently. These days, the students were all suspicious of her. She was afraid, afraid that this paper tiger would be exposed, as if an unfortunate thing was about to befall her.

"(Someone is looking for you in the reception room)." She was suddenly startled by this crisp voice, but she didn't know who was looking for her.

She slowly ran to the reception room. "(Ah)." She let out a surprised and ashamed cry.

"(Oh, Yindi, last year because you wanted to make a short shirt, I pawned my several foot warmers. Now, now the term has expired and they are gone. What should I do? How will I keep warm this winter? Like someone as old as me, my child, you should always think of me, because pawning these foot warmers was for you)," an old woman in ragged clothes said with tears as soon as she saw her.

Her eyes went black, and the surrounding air was filled with mocking voices.

Youth Garden Contribution Guidelines

(1) The text should be about the discussion of youth issues, domestic and foreign school or student news, essays, descriptions of school life, essays, etc. The style is not limited.

(2) The drawings should be limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) Photos that qualify are those about youth life (such as sports, travel, sightseeing, drama performances, speeches, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements. Both individuals and groups are welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) The number of words in each article should not exceed two thousand.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and do not be sloppy. Western text can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not draw drawings with blue ink, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please indicate that the submissions should be sent to the Youth Garden Editorial Department.

Shanghai Market

Calligraphy and Painting News

Yi Cheng Calligraphy and Painting Society declared that the establishment of the society was originally to promote art and propagate the works of artists. In addition to various exhibitions that have been held four times, the personal calligraphy and painting exhibition of Yang Du from Xiangtan is now being held. According to Mr. Yang's word Xizi, he is an apprentice of Xiangqi Old Man, and his poems, books, and paintings are called the three best. More than 50 pieces of calligraphy and painting currently displayed in the society are recent masterpieces. It has been determined that the sixth and seventh exhibitions will be continued by Bi Xiufang from Wujin and the Drama Calligraphy and Painting Association. At that time, the grand occasion will be easy to predict.

Yu Jianhua, a native of Lu Jumen, has a fondness for calligraphy and painting. He was imbued with family studies in his youth and became proficient in the six methods when he grew up. He used to study in Beijing under the late calligrapher Chen Shizeng, and he gained his heart. He liked to travel and his footprints were all over the north and south. Wherever he went, he must write with a pen and inkstone, wading through mountains and rivers, exhausting his secluded victory, and taking his natural chalk book to benefit the hills in his chest. What he saw was extensive and the artistic conception was beyond the comprehension of the ancients. He gained a great deal from the help of landscapes. He is proficient in all kinds of calligraphy, including regular script, cursive script, official script, and seal script. He is not limited by one family. He is especially good at bronze inscriptions, from Shang divination shells to Mao Gong Ding, San Shi Pan, Shi Gu Wen, Qin Quan and Han tiles. He is proficient in all of them. The iron paintings and silver hooks are like painting sand, like printing mud, like a broken hairpin, like a trace of house leakage. The ancient style is dense and lush, elegant and robust. The running cursive script is like Jin and Tang dynasties, swift and smooth, with the momentum of dragons soaring and phoenixes flying. The flower temple uses strong strokes and gorgeous colors to write the branches and leaves in the wind, and the buds are in full bloom, all of which exhaust the state of things. In addition to Qing Teng, Bai Yang, Futang and Nantian, a banner is set up. Landscapes initially learn from Shen Shitian, then learn from Mei Yuangong, and then come to Shanghai to make Gong Banqian famous at the time. More recently, they have been flooded with the works of various schools of Song and Yuan Dynasties, and they have explored the works of Shi Tao and Shi Xi especially carefully. Therefore, the works contain an attitude of ah na in the midst of vigor and strength, and an air of vigor and strength in the midst of elegance. They must take the essence of the ancients and not stick to the ancient appearance. In addition, the famous mountains and rivers that have been traveled to all over the world, the vast atmosphere of their opening and closing, rushes to the bottom of the wrist, so they can get rid of the constant path and surpass the current trends. He is proficient in writing and has a wealth of works. He is also proficient in Western methods and design. He is currently the director and professor of the Chinese Painting Department of Xinhua Art College. He is enthusiastic, so many scholars have become talents. He is also a class teacher in the liberal arts of the Patriotic Girls' School. He is young and strong, and his aspirations have not yet been realized. Who can measure his future achievements? Now it is scheduled to be held at the Xizang Ningbo Township Association for three days on the 15th, 16th and 17th of this month.

The entire Ziegfeld Follies dance troupe, filled with beautiful women, will perform. Mary Eaton, the star of "The Charming Bachelor," plays the lead role. In addition, Rudy Valle, the modern music king, sings moving love songs in "Just a Vagabond Lover," and the comedian Eddie Cantor performs a tailor shop scene. Several dance scenes are rendered in vivid color. In addition to this feature film, the latest sound newsreel will be shown, featuring the world tennis stars Tilden and Cochet in a tennis final.

Great China Film Company announces that their long-awaited fashion, martial arts, love, and adventure epic "The King of Magic" will soon be completed. The scene of a fierce fight was filmed yesterday, showcasing the most dangerous feats. The villain's assistant, Huang Yong (played by Tang Yunqing), is chased by the righteous magician Shi Buping (played by Chen Qiuhua). Huang Yong, unable to escape, jumps from a building over fifty feet high. This is just one example of the extraordinary performance. It is easy to imagine the exciting content of this film with many unique highlights.

Yaru Opera House in Deren Lane, at the intersection of Zhejiang Road and Tianjin Road, announces that this opera house is organized by Chen Guoqin, Huang Jincheng, Shen Tingzhang, etc., and has hired Shen Shaoting and Wang Kuiyuan as teachers, and Dong Guiting and Meng Zhongqing as musicians. Dozens of male and female members have joined. A rehearsal with costumes and makeup is scheduled for the middle of next month, which will be a grand occasion.

(1) Please indicate "Shanghai Market Department Received" on all submissions from businesses, doctors, film companies, theaters, calligraphers, and painters.

(2) Please affix a seal to all submissions from businesses, film companies, theaters, calligraphers, painters, and doctors to serve as verification. Otherwise, we regret that we cannot publish them.

(3) According to the usual practice, a small fee is paid for lengthy film reviews, which remains at one yuan per thousand words.

Shen Bao Pictorial Weekly

(1) General Uriburu, the Provisional President of Argentina (*) being welcomed by the crowd during a victory parade in the City of Silver, after overthrowing the government of Irigoyen. Seated to his right is Colonel Marile, who supports Uriburu.

In South America, three armed revolutions have occurred in succession in the recent mid-March. The presidents of Bolivia (Salas), Peru (Leguia), and Argentina (Irigoyen) have been successively overthrown. Other Central and South American countries are also brewing trouble, and there is a danger of imminent explosion. The reason is not political but economic. In a word, it is due to the low value of exported goods. This is especially true in Argentina for meat and grains. Because the republics of the Americas are interspersed with conflicting parties and factions, and the United States of North America uses economic expansion to promote Pan-Americanism, thereby manipulating and oppressing them. The government has no good way to remedy this during this time of worldwide overproduction and surging unemployment. Those in the fields have something to use as an excuse, and storms are rising.

(2) A view of the Mayo Palace of the Brazilian government from a foreign platform. In front is the Independence Memorial, with a white flag already hung on top.

(3) Dr. Irigoyen, President of Argentina, was originally a history teacher. In 1902 and 1905, he was the leader of revolutions. In 1916 and 1928, he was re-elected twice. Now, due to the revolutionary wave, he was forced to resign on September 6. The government and congress were dissolved and replaced by a military government.

(4) Bolivian students gathered in front of the statue of General Stone on June 4 to commemorate his death anniversary. A cabinet member wanted to address them, but they shot at him, and the revolutionary storm began in the capital.

(5) The private residence of Bolivian President Salas being destroyed by the people before the establishment of the military government.

(6) Augusto Leguia, President of Peru, seized power by force and implemented a dictatorship for ten years. Now, he has been overthrown by the revolutionary army. On August 24, he fled by ship and is now exiled to the isolated island of San Lorenzo. The Peruvian people hate Leguia for his wealth and have destroyed his residence in the capital. However, the new government rises and falls quickly, causing losses to overseas Chinese shops.

(7) The Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Sir Eric Drummond, will tour South America to promote South American people's attention to the League of Nations. However, he will only visit coastal countries. Bolivia and Uruguay may not be able to go.

(8) The International Education Bureau of the League of Nations held a lecture meeting in Geneva. The Chinese Ministry of Education specially sent Mr. Guo Zixiong (*) and Mr. Dan Yinsheng (○) as representatives to attend.

(9) Italian Prime Minister Mussolini gave a speech at the Fascist Party's march on Rome anniversary celebration on October 28, advocating for the revision of the peace treaty and subtly attacking France. He said that the ideas and methods of Fascism can eventually reach the whole of Europe. German newspapers said that his speech was like throwing a bomb into European politics, and the stock market was affected. This is a family photo of Mussolini. He is holding his third son, Romano. To his left is his wife, holding their young daughter Maria. To his right is his eldest daughter, Aida, and next to her is the Italian Consul General in Shanghai, Mr. Nobili and his wife, and finally his second son Vittorio, and his eldest son Bruno.

— (Wang Xiaoxie)

A Visit to Petrarch's Spring

— Hua Lin

The Italian poet who initiated the Renaissance, Petrarch (1304-1374), was born in Arezzo, Italy. His father, a member of the White faction, was exiled abroad. The poet traveled around and met a beautiful woman named Laura in Avignon, southern France, and fell deeply in love with her. He then wrote love poems to praise her. The poetry collection is divided into two volumes: Before and After Laura's Death. The sorrowful and lingering feelings in the latter volume are even more exquisite. The poet chose to live near the spring of Vaucluse in the mountains near the famous city of Avignon. This spring is under a cliff. The old spring has dried up, leaving traces. The new spring gushes out from the chaotic rocks, stirring up snow-white waves and forming a long, winding path. There is the fragrance of flowers on both banks of the stream. Beside the stream is Petrarch's former residence. Ancient books are displayed in the room, and a portrait of the beautiful Laura adorns the walls. This shows that the poet's life was turbulent and displaced, and he cherished the sorrow of the country's demise. He suffered the same unfortunate fate as Dante. The world is surging forward in pursuit of power, and there is no one to share a word with. Only the illusion of beauty can be used to tell his secrets and entrust his deep feelings. In addition, there is the clear spring in the valley, and the wind and moon in the mountains. The poet soothes and adds color to the mountains and lakes with his constant singing. When I visited the Avignon Art Museum, I saw broken columns and drooping willows in the courtyard, which are Laura's tomb. I couldn't bear to leave, so I looked back and transformed into spring mud to accompany this ancient tomb. I am willing to transform into a cuckoo, constantly singing in the willow branches. Because of the poet, the beautiful Laura, and the spring of Vaucluse, it is immortal.

(1) Petrarch

(2) Laura

(3) Petrarch's former residence near the spring

(4) Laura's tomb

(5) The long flow of the spring water of Vaucluse

(6) The gushing spring of Vaucluse
